                    id="post-2294">
                        \n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="headline_area">
                            \n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <h1 class="entry-title">Coffee
                            Caramels</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <p class="headline_meta">by <span class=
                            "author vcard fn">Eddy Van Damme</span> on
                            <abbr class="published" title="2013-06-24">June 24,
                            2013</abbr></p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="format_text entry-content">
                            \n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/Coffee-caramels.jpg">
                            <img alt="Coffee caramels" class=
                            "alignleft size-large wp-image-2295" height="680"
                            src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/Coffee-caramels-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="1024" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>Caramels are much desired the world over and can
                            be made in many different flavors. While vanilla
                            and chocolate are the most popular ones, coffee
                            pairs exceptionally well with the buttery tones of
                            caramel.</p>\n
                            <p>The coffee caramels can be wrapped in cellophane
                            as shown in On Baking, or can be dipped in milk or
                            dark chocolate couverture and finished with a touch
                            of fleur de sel, if so desired.</p>\n
                            <p>Coffee Caramel</p>\n
                            <p>A chewy caramel that does not stick to
                            teeth.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n
                            <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
                                <tbody>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">1 x
                                        recipe</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Caramel
                                        candies, On Baking 3, page 730</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">1 x
                                        recipe</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">1.5
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Coffee
                                        extract</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">45 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                </tbody>
                            </table>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <ol>
                                <li style="list-style: none">\n</li>
                                <li>Prepare recipe as indicated. Add coffee
                                extract at 245F (118C). Cook further until
                                caramel reaches 245F (118C) again. For a firmer
                                caramel cook a few degrees higher.\n</li>
                            </ol>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/caramels.jpg">
                            <img alt="caramels" class=
                            "alignleft size-large wp-image-2296" height="680"
                            src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/06/caramels-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="1024" /></a></p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t

                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>The Coffee Caramel had a chew filling
                                    and with a sweet of milk chocolate.</p>\n

                                    <div class="sfw-comment-author vcard">
                                        \n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt="\'\'" class=
                                        "\'avatar" height="\'68\'" src=

                                        "">December 10, 2013 at 6:20
                                        pm</time></a> <span class=
                                        "says">said:</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t

                                    <!-- .comment-author .vcard -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t

                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>&#8220;A chewy caramel that does not
                                    stick to teeth&#8221;; that in itself makes
                                    it delicious before even having tasted it.
                                    I do enjoy salted caramel, so I may try it
                                    with that. And it seems a good idea to top
                                    it with pretzel bit for that extra salted
                                    bit instead of just using salted
                                    caramel.</p>\n
                                </div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t

                        <div class="headline_area">
                            \n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <h1 class="entry-title">Artisanal Belgian Chocolate
                            Truffles</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <p class="headline_meta">by <span class=
                            "author vcard fn">Eddy Van Damme</span> on
                            <abbr class="published" title="2013-05-20">May 20,
                            2013</abbr></p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="format_text entry-content">
                            \n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Belgian-truffle-recipe.jpg">
                            <img alt="Belgian truffle recipe" class=
                            "alignleft wp-image-2282" height="544" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Belgian-truffle-recipe-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="819" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>Truffles can be made either by using heavy
                            cream, chocolate and a sweetener or are made with
                            butter, chocolate and a sweetener. Both can be
                            delicious and have their own distinct
                            characteristic. If you desire to make truffles with
                            well pronounced flavor (from liquor, extracts, tea,
                            coffee etc) then butter based truffles may be a
                            good choice. The creamed butter mixture, which is
                            consequently light and airy makes it possible for
                            flavors to really shine through, which can be a
                            challenge when using bitter chocolate.</p>\n
                            <p>These truffles are flavored with homemade coffee
                            extract and sprinkled with nougatine.</p>\n
                            <p>Artisanal Belgian Truffles | Coffee
                            Nougatine</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n
                            <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
                                <tbody>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                    </tr>
                                </tbody>
                            </table>\n
                            <p>Yield: 60
                            truffles</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n
                            <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
                                <tbody>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">8. 5
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Unsalted
                                        butter, best quality</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">250 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">3 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"><a href=
                                        "http://www.chefeddy.com/2009/11/invert-sugar/"
                                        target="_blank">Invert sugar</a></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">90 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">10 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Dark
                                        Chocolate couverture (54%)</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">300 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">7 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Milk
                                        chocolate (38% cocoa)</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">210 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">1.5
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"><a href=
                                        "http://www.chefeddy.com/2011/09/coffee-extract/"
                                        target="_blank">Coffee extract</a></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">45 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">1 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Coffee
                                        liquor or dark Rum</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">30 ml</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">1 lb 8
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Dark
                                        Couverture (54%-64%)</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">750</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                    </tr>
                                </tbody>
                            </table>\n
                            <ol>
                                <li style="list-style: none">\n</li>
                                <li>Mix butter until creamy, add invert sugar
                                and cream more.\n</li>
                                <li>Melt first listed dark and milk chocolate
                                to 95\xc2\xb0F (34\xc2\xb0C) and at this
                                temperature to creamed butter. Mix well and add
                                coffee extract and liquor and mix until
                                combined.\n</li>
                                <li>Let mixture set for approximately 30
                                minutes or until crystallization starts to take
                                place.\n</li>
                                <li>Pipe into even mounds. Sprinkle with very
                                thin rolled pieces of <a href=
                                "http://www.chefeddy.com/2009/10/nougatine/"
                                target="_blank">nougatine</a>. Do not place the
                                truffles in a refrigerator. Let set in a cool
                                area until fully crystallized, about 2
                                hours.\n</li>
                                <li>Temper couverture chocolate as shown on
                                this site and dip truffles, drop onto quality
                                cocoa powder.\n</li>
                                <li>Carefully roll the dipped truffles into
                                cocoa powder ensuring not to stick the fork
                                into the truffle itself.\n</li>
                                <li>When firm shake off extra cocoa powder and
                                place in a refrigerator. Serve at room
                                temperature for full flavor experience.\n</li>
                            </ol>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Belgian-truffles.jpg">
                            <img alt="Belgian truffles" class=
                            "alignleft wp-image-2283" height="544" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Belgian-truffles-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="819" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n\t\t\t\t

                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>These were the first thing we made,
                                    definitely did not turn out looking like
                                    yours but they were really good, although I
                                    think the pure cocoa powder we rolled them
                                    in may have been a little
                                    overpowering.</p>\n
                                </div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t

                                    <!-- .comment-author .vcard -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t
                                </div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t
                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>&#8220;If you desire to make truffles
                                    with well pronounced flavor (from liquor,
                                    extracts, tea, coffee etc) then butter
                                    based truffles may be a good choice&#8221;
                                    is such a great tip, because I would not
                                    have known which was better otherwise. As
                                    much as I love dark chocolates, I do also
                                    like my fair share of liquor filling in
                                    chocolates; it would be fun to make it with
                                    interesting fillings like sake, or a sure
                                    hit filling like irish cream liquor.</p>\n
                                </div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t

                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>Hi Chefeddy<br />
                                    \nI thought that cream based ganaches need
                                    a certain percentage of invert sugar (or
                                    glucose syrup) to control available water
                                    and sugar crystalization. I was wondering
                                    why do you use relatively large amount of
                                    invert sugar in a butter ganache (without
                                    extracts it would be extremely low water
                                    content)?</p>\n

                    \n\n\t\t\t
                    <div class=
                    "post_box top post-2260 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-plated_dessert"
                    id="post-2260">
                        \n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="headline_area">
                            \n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <h1 class="entry-title">Lemon Curd
                            Plated</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <p class="headline_meta">by <span class=
                            "author vcard fn">Eddy Van Damme</span> on
                            <abbr class="published" title="2013-05-06">May 6,
                            2013</abbr></p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="format_text entry-content">
                            \n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/lemon-curd.jpg">
                            <img alt="lemon curd" class=
                            "alignleft wp-image-2261" height="558" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/lemon-curd.jpg"
                            width="840" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>Lemon, lime or passion fruit curd can easily be
                            turned into delicious desserts which are much
                            appreciated by our customers. Curds made over Bain
                            Marie can be a lengthy process which oftentimes
                            keeps us from making it. The good news is that this
                            formula allows for quick results with unsurpassed
                            smoothness.</p>\n
                            <p>Use it for sandwiching petit four, serve with
                            scones, filling for tarts or as shown here as a
                            plated dessert.</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>Assembly:</p>\n
                            <p>Prepare curd and pour in frame. Set in
                            refrigerator for one hour and then place in freezer
                            until solid.</p>\n
                            <p>Prepare meringue and streusel.</p>\n
                            <p>Cut frozen curd quickly into desired size. Place
                            on plate. Allow for defrosting, about 5
                            minutes.</p>\n
                            <p>Decorate with baked meringue, streusel, berries
                            etc.</p>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/lemon-curd-plated-dessert.jpg">
                            <img alt="lemon curd plated dessert" class=
                            "alignleft wp-image-2269" height="615" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/lemon-curd-plated-dessert.jpg"
                            width="926" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>Quick Lime Curd | Quick lemon curd</p>\n
                            <p>This recipe is from <i>On Baking (Named in
                            Europe the best professional book of the world)</i>
                            published with permission from Pearson Prentice
                            Hall</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>Yield: 1 lb 4 oz (619
                            g)</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n
                            <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
                                <tbody>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">4 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Lime or
                                        lemon juice</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">120 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">6.5
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Extra fine
                                        granulated sugar</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">195 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">0.14
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">zest</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">4 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">4 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Eggs</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">120 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">6 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Unsalted
                                        butter*, very soft</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">180 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                </tbody>
                            </table>\n
                            <ol>
                                <li style="list-style: none">\n</li>
                                <li>To use curd as shown in picture use a
                                square frame with approximate size of 9 x 9
                                inch (23 x 23 cm). Wrap plastic food wrap
                                tightly around frame to create a bottom. Set
                                aside on a baking sheet.\n</li>
                                <li><i></i><i>Curd will set properly when made
                                as indicated. Adding one sheet of bloomed
                                gelatin (after cooking process) or one extra
                                egg white (along with whole eggs) may be
                                helpful for plating purpose as this will
                                provide a slightly firmer set.</i>\n</li>
                                <li>Bring citrus juice with half of sugar to a
                                boil.\n</li>
                                <li>Meanwhile in a bowl whisk eggs with
                                remaining sugar until well combined but not
                                mixed to a thick ribbon.\n</li>
                                <li>Temper the egg mixture with a third of
                                boiling above. Pour the tempered mixture into
                                boiling juice and whisk vigorously until
                                boiling and thickened, about a minute. (For
                                large batches increase the boiling time)\n</li>
                                <li>Remove from heat and cool on an ice bath to
                                120\xc2\xb0F (50\xc2\xb0C)\n</li>
                                <li>Add the butter in increments, stirring well
                                with a spatula or add the butter using an
                                immersion blender.\n</li>
                                <li>Pour immediately into frame or use in
                                glasses, tart shells etc.\n</li>
                            </ol>\n
                            <p>*use high quality butter (82% butterfat) for
                            best results.</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>French Style Meringue</p>\n
                            <p>On Baking 3, page 410.</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <ol>
                                <li style="list-style: none">\n</li>
                                <li>Prepare meringue and pipe 1 inch (3 cm)
                                long tubes with a small pastry tip.\n</li>
                                <li>Using a spoon or small pastry spatula
                                flatten the tube to create an organic
                                shape.\n</li>
                                <li>Sprinkle with unsweetened coconut if
                                desired.\n</li>
                                <li>Bake at 225\xc2\xb0F (110\xc2\xb0C) for
                                about 45 minutes or until crisp. Keep from
                                humidity.\n</li>
                            </ol>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Meringue-decorations.jpg">
                            <img alt="Meringue decorations" class=
                            "alignleft wp-image-2273" height="612" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Meringue-decorations-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="922" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t
                    </div>\n\n\t\t\t

                                    <p>Thank you for showing us how to
                                    elegantly plate a seemingly simple lemon
                                    curd. Is it possible to use finely chopped
                                    nuts (like pistachio) instead of coconut? I
                                    personally enjoy the flavor combination of
                                    lemon, blueberry, and basil. Would you
                                    recommend using basil oil or extract to add
                                    basil flavor to the meringue? If not, I
                                    guess striping the piping bag with
                                    gel-paste food coloring to give the
                                    meringue some color is my creative
                                    contribution. Again, thank you.</p>\n

                    \n\n\t\t\t
                    <div class=
                    "post_box top post-2231 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-plated_dessert"
                    id="post-2231">
                        \n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="headline_area">
                            \n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <h1 class="entry-title">Ghent</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <p class="headline_meta">by <span class=
                            "author vcard fn">Eddy Van Damme</span> on
                            <abbr class="published" title="2013-04-22">April
                            22, 2013</abbr></p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="format_text entry-content">
                            \n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/04/ghent/ghent/" rel=
                            "attachment wp-att-2232"><img alt="Ghent." class=
                            "alignleft size-large wp-image-2232" height="768"
                            src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/Ghent.-1024x768.jpg"
                            width="1024" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>Ghent, place of my birth.</p>\n
                            <p>With thousands of you visiting chefeddy.com on a
                            daily basis I thought it may be a good idea sharing
                            something more than another recipe. After all,
                            being in the food industry may spark an interest in
                            visiting Belgium some day. Ghent Belgium is rated #
                            3 on National Geographic\xe2\x80\x99s Travelers
                            list of beautiful historic places. Ghent is nestled
                            between Brussels and Bruges, about a good 40 minute
                            drive either way. Many tourists only visit the
                            named above, too bad for them, as the Historic
                            center of Ghent boasts a complete different type of
                            \xe2\x80\x9cfeel\xe2\x80\x9d and architecture than
                            that of Brussels. It is a must see indeed. The
                            historic center is car free thus you walk along the
                            people who live and work in Ghent and who will
                            quickly make you feel as you already belong. This
                            is NOT a city where you feel as a tourist who MUST
                            visit or buy something to absorb the place. Ghent
                            will slow you down and will make you take your time
                            to enjoy a patio with good coffee, Belgian beer,
                            lunch, dinner, dessert etc. Stay as long as you
                            want on the patio, no one will rush you as the Gent
                            HORECA (HOtel, REstaurant, CAf\xc3\xa9) owners will
                            respect and be truly grateful for your visit.</p>\n
                            <p>It is true that you can eat exceptionally well
                            in Belgium, (the amount of Michelin rated star
                            restaurants per capita is extraordinarily high).
                            But most of us do not frequent these on a daily
                            basis. When we are in the historic area of Ghent we
                            frequent many restaurants and many are very good,
                            but everyone has favorites and I am sharing mine.
                            For coffee we like to stop at 3,14 (Pi) at the
                            Groentemarkt. Delicious cappuccino and coffee
                            served in a friendly manner in a cool interior make
                            it a great spot indeed. Picture below 3,14</p>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/04/ghent/attachment/314/"
                            rel="attachment wp-att-2234"><img alt="3,14" class=
                            "alignleft size-full wp-image-2234" height="480"
                            src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/314.jpg"
                            width="640" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>For lunch or dinner we favor restaurant The
                            Graslei found on n\xc2\xb07 of the street of the
                            same name. When weather is good, take a seat on the
                            breathtaking patio overlooking water and buildings
                            dating from the 13 th century. If the weather is
                            slightly cold, you can still sit on the patio as
                            luxury blankets are on each and every chair and
                            outdoor heaters will be on. Inside, the
                            d\xc3\xa9cor is beautiful, immaculate and stylishly
                            Belgian. Retaining parts of the old building mixed
                            with the new. The food you say? Always delicious
                            and very generous and will make you want to come
                            again, even the same day. Ilse, the proprietor will
                            greet you with tremendous enthusiasm and Jonas and
                            the other attentive wait staff will serve you
                            gracefully and respectfully. Plenty of excellent
                            wine choices at the <a href=
                            "http://www.restaurantdegraslei.be/">Graslei</a>,
                            although for lunch or in the afternoon on the patio
                            I may reach for one of Belgium\xe2\x80\x99s most
                            delicious beers, a Trippel Karmeliet, a beer I also
                            use on occasion to cook savory dishes.</p>\n
                            <p><img alt="DE-GRASLEI-004" height="544" src=
                            "http://www.restaurantdegraslei.be/cache/widgetkit/gallery/1/DE-GRASLEI-004-5cd833dc68.jpg"
                            width="816" /></p>\n
                            <p>Picture above: Courtesy Restaurant Graslei</p>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/04/ghent/dsc03258/"
                            rel="attachment wp-att-2247"><img alt="DSC03258"
                            class="alignleft wp-image-2247" height="648" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/DSC03258.jpg"
                            width="864" /></a></p>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/04/ghent/ghent-2/"
                            rel="attachment wp-att-2245"><img alt="Ghent"
                            class="alignleft size-full wp-image-2245" height=
                            "480" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/Ghent.jpg"
                            width="640" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n

                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>Ghent has a restaurant that locals are
                                    willing to eat the meals. Chef Eddy, this
                                    is where you were born and raised before
                                    coming to the United States of America.
                                    Now, I understand where you were from and
                                    this is why you became a pastry chef. I
                                    might go to your place for a vacation and
                                    it has a history. The 6th picture I saw is
                                    a remnant of the catacombs. This catacomb
                                    in Ghent is made of real life stones. Fifth
                                    picture has a similarity of the river from
                                    Amsterdam and France. It is a clean
                                    environment to walk, explore, and each
                                    house is very old. The house in picture
                                    number 4 is made of white stone and dark
                                    wood. It is very scary to go inside the
                                    catacombs when lights are out. Also, it is
                                    expensive. Thanks for showing me this
                                    pictures.</p>\n

                                    sounds so wonderful and looks so beautiful,
                                    it&#8217;s no wonder it&#8217;s rated #3 on
                                    National Geographic\xe2\x80\x99s travelers
                                    list.</p>\n
                                </div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t

                        <div class="headline_area">
                            \n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <h1 class="entry-title">Easy
                            Tiramisu</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <p class="headline_meta">by <span class=
                            "author vcard fn">Eddy Van Damme</span> on
                            <abbr class="published" title="2013-04-09">April 9,
                            2013</abbr></p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="format_text entry-content">
                            \n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/04/tiramisu-easy/tiramisu-2/"
                            rel="attachment wp-att-2209"><img alt="Tiramisu"
                            class="alignleft wp-image-2209" height="612" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/Tiramisu-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="922" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>When preparing desserts for huge events, having
                            enough equipment can be an issue. Who has,
                            let\xe2\x80\x99s say 800 individual rings
                            handy?\xc2\xa0Therefore I like to teach students
                            ways of using ordinary equipment and yet, still
                            obtaining stylish results. One example is featured
                            here. A standard American type sheet pan is used to
                            obtain this dessert. First thin <a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2009/11/how-to-make-ladyfingers/"
                            target="_blank">ladyfinger batter</a> was spread
                            onto a sheet pan and baked. Once cooled and
                            released is was placed on a plastic food film lined
                            sheet pan. Moistened with <a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2009/11/tiramisu/" target=
                            "_blank">coffee syrup</a> and then topped with
                            mascarpone cream. After freezing it was released
                            from the pan and cut into rectangle sized
                            shapes.</p>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/04/easy-tiramisu/dsc_0356/"
                            rel="attachment wp-att-2221"><img alt="DSC_0356"
                            class="alignleft wp-image-2221" height="544" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/DSC_0356-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="819" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>Mascarpone cream for Tiramisu</p>\n
                            <p>Yield: 33 cm x 45 cm (13 x 18 inch) size sheet
                            pan.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n
                            <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
                                <tbody>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">8)</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Egg
                                        yolks</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">8</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">4 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Water</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">120
                                        ml</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">6 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Extra fine
                                        granulated sugar</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">180 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">4</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Gelatin
                                        leaves (optional*)</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">4</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">16 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Mascarpone
                                        cheese</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">480 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">2 tsp</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Vanilla
                                        extract (Optional)</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">10 ml</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">12 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Heavy
                                        cream</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">360 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                    </tr>
                                </tbody>
                            </table>\n
                            <p>*If using this cream to fill in verrines
                            (glasses) gelatin can be omitted.</p>\n
                            <ol>
                                <li style="list-style: none">\n</li>
                                <li>Place gelatin leaves in very cold water and
                                set aside.\n</li>
                                <li>In a cold bowl whisk heavy cream to very
                                soft, barely a ribbon consistency.
                                Over-whipping will result in poor results. Set
                                aside.\n</li>
                                <li>Fill a saucepan with a small amount of
                                water and bring to a boil and then turn to a
                                low simmer.\xc2\xa0 In a bowl whisk together
                                egg yolks and measured water. Add sugar and
                                whisk well. Place the bowl over the simmering
                                water and whisk constantly until the yolk
                                mixture reaches at least 165\xc2\xb0F
                                (74\xc2\xb0C). Remove from heat.\n</li>
                                <li>Remove the gelatin leaves from the water
                                and squeeze well to remove excess water. Whisk
                                the gelatin into the yolk mixture. Add the
                                mascarpone cheese and vanilla extract and whisk
                                smooth.\n</li>
                                <li>Add the soft whipped heavy cream and gently
                                fold into the above using a spatula. Fill into
                                the mold immediately.\n</li>
                            </ol>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t
                    </div>\n\n\t\t\t

                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>Chef, i found most of the tiramisu sold
                                    around Houston are way too fluffy. I used
                                    to make mine the easy way, by mixing
                                    mascarpone cheese, egg yolk &amp; vanilla
                                    sugar together. Then soaked my ladyfingers
                                    with strong dark coffee &amp; some
                                    Bailey&#8217;s <img alt=":-)" class=
                                    "wp-smiley" src=
                                    "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png"
                                    style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" />
                                    Keep it refrigerate overnight for a
                                    cheesecake consistency&#8230; yummy! What
                                    you think?</p>\n

                                    <p>Ever since i made this my mother never
                                    went back to cheesecake. Masarcopne chesse
                                    is the perfect texture with out the strong
                                    cream cheese flavor. Comparing to
                                    chessecake i like the crust separately
                                    cheese baked off and crust baked off. Im
                                    not a fan of a soggy crust and it is a
                                    fabulous idea to plate tiramisu this way
                                    since we do have to soak the crust it
                                    doesnt have to be soggy! this is a perfect
                                    mix.</p>\n

                                    <p>When we made this in class with the
                                    glass, I liked the creaminess of the
                                    tiramisu but I don&#8217;t think I would
                                    soak the lady fingers with the coffee

                                \n\t\t\t\t\t
                                <div class="sfw-comment-meta">
                                    \n\t\t\t\t\t\t
                                    <div class="sfw-comment-author vcard">
                                        \n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<img alt="\'\'" class=
                                        "\'avatar" height="\'68\'" src=
                                        "/'http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f2b81ab637e94cf5f5becd7abc9f284f?s=68&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g/'"
                                        srcset=
                                        "\'http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f2b81ab637e94cf5f5becd7abc9f284f?s=136&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g"
                                        width="\'68\'" /><span class=
                                        "sfw-fn">Eileen Mier</span> on <a href=
                                        "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/04/easy-tiramisu/comment-page-1/#comment-25788">
                                        <time datetime=
                                        "2013-06-30T22:39:46+00:00" pubdate=
                                        "">June 30, 2013 at 10:39 pm</time></a>
                                        <span class=
                                        "says">said:</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t
                                    </div>
                                    <!-- .comment-author .vcard -->\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t
                                </div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t
                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>Tiramisu is hands down one of my
                                    favorite desserts, but sometimes recipes
                                    I&#8217;ve tried before were a bit heavy
                                    handed with the coffee, what with the
                                    ladyfingers being dipped/soaked in coffee
                                    syrup and liquor and coffee being mixed in
                                    with the marscapone. I like how you had us
                                    brush our baked ladyfinger batter with the
                                    coffee syrup, didn&#8217;t have us add
                                    coffee to the cream so that we could
                                    &#8220;let the marscapone shine&#8221;.
                                    This was absolutely delightful.</p>\n
                                </div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t

                    \n\n\t\t\t
                    <div class=
                    "post_box top post-2198 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cake category-individual-desserts"
                    id="post-2198">
                        \n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="headline_area">
                            \n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <h1 class="entry-title">Creamy
                            Cheesecake</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t
                            <p class="headline_meta">by <span class=
                            "author vcard fn">Eddy Van Damme</span> on
                            <abbr class="published" title="2013-03-18">March
                            18, 2013</abbr></p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t\t
                        <div class="format_text entry-content">
                            \n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/03/creamy-cheesecake/cheesecake/"
                            rel="attachment wp-att-2199"><img alt="cheesecake"
                            class="alignleft wp-image-2199" height="544" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/03/cheesecake-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="819" /></a></p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>Philadelphia Cream cheese is indeed one of the
                            few cheeses which make it possible to create
                            smooth, delectable and creamy cheesecake. However,
                            using a large percentage of this type of cheese for
                            the production of cheesecake, can result in cakes
                            which tend to be a bit heavy for today\xe2\x80\x99s
                            consumer. Therefore I prefer to mix a rather large
                            amount of Greek Yogurt into the cheese mixture. It
                            makes it lighter, while at the same time making it
                            superbly creamy. Greek yogurt also provides a
                            slight tangy flavor found in cream cheese.</p>\n
                            <p>When I teach cheesecakes, I have noticed that
                            students tend to pay close attention to the demos
                            and instruction. As is the case with so many
                            things, something as simple as cheesecake is not
                            that simple at all. Oftentimes cheesecakes result
                            in products which \xe2\x80\x9cglue\xe2\x80\x9d to
                            our palate.</p>\n
                            <p>Key things to remember when making
                            cheesecake:</p>\n
                            <ol>
                                <li style="list-style: none">\n</li>
                                <li>Use cream cheese which is at room
                                temperature. It cuts the amount of time that
                                the mixture will be mixed. Long mixing times
                                breaks down cream cheese and results in a thin
                                batter and consequently a crumbly
                                cheesecake.\n</li>
                                <li>Mix on lowest speed possible. Mixing on
                                medium or high speed incorporates air cells.
                                This \xe2\x80\x9csouffl\xc3\xa9s\xe2\x80\x9d
                                the cheesecake during baking, but since there
                                is no starch present, it will collapse when
                                removed from oven. This makes it not only
                                unsightly, but it also creates a dry feel in
                                the mouth.\n</li>
                                <li>Use a Bain Marie and low temperatures when
                                baking. It creates a superior smooth textured
                                cheesecake.\n</li>
                                <li>This recipe does not allow freezing of the
                                cake.\n</li>
                            </ol>\n
                            <p><a href=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/03/creamy-cheesecake/cheese-cake/"
                            rel="attachment wp-att-2200"><img alt="cheese cake"
                            class="alignleft wp-image-2200" height="544" src=
                            "http://www.chefeddy.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/03/cheese-cake-1024x680.jpg"
                            width="819" /></a></p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n
                            <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
                                <tbody>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                </tbody>
                            </table>\n
                            <p>Cheesecake</p>\n
                            <p>Yield: 12-14
                            servings.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n
                            <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
                                <tbody>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">1 lb 8
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Cream
                                        cheese, Philadelphia</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">720 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">9 oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Extra fine
                                        granulated sugar</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">270 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">5</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Large
                                        eggs</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">5</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">1tsp</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Vanilla
                                        extract</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">5 ml</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">.25
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Lemon
                                        zest</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">9 g</td>
                                    </tr>
                                    <tr>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160">1 lb 4
                                        oz</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="210">Fage,
                                        Greek Yogurt</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">600 g</td>
                                    </tr>

                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>

                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>

                                        <td valign="top" width="210"></td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109"></td>

                                        <td valign="top" width="160"></td>

                                        <td valign="top" width="210">
                                        &nbsp;</td>
                                        <td valign="top" width="109">
                                        &nbsp;</td>

                                        <td valign="top" width="160">

                            </table>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <ol>
                                <li style="list-style: none">\n</li>
                                <li>Choose a 20 cm (8 inch) spring form pan
                                wrapped in 3 ply aluminum foil or for a plated
                                dessert use a frame placed on 3 ply aluminum
                                foil. Brush with melted butter and sprinkle
                                with extra granulated sugar. Set aside.\n</li>
                                <li>On lowest speed using a paddle attachment
                                mix room temperature cheese and sugar. When
                                smooth and lump free ad one egg at a time
                                waiting for previous added egg to be fully
                                incorporated.\n</li>
                                <li>Add vanilla, lemon zest and yogurt and mix
                                to combine.\n</li>
                                <li>Pour into buttered and sugared molds of
                                choice and place in Bain Marie, bake at
                                325\xc2\xb0F (160\xc2\xb0C) until center of
                                cheesecake no longer trembles. Time will depend
                                on pan used.\n</li>
                                <li>Unmold next day onto a prebaked crust of
                                choice.\n</li>
                            </ol>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n
                            <p>&nbsp;</p>\n\t\t\t\t
                        </div>\n\t\t\t

                                <div class="sfw-comment-content">
                                    <p>In my group we did two cheesecake. The
                                    first one we did we use this recipe and the
                                    second one someone in my group forgot to
                                    add vanilla to the mixture, and the flavor
                                    for both cheesecake were completely
                                    different. The flavor for the first
                                    cheesecake was better than the second one.
                                    For my experience, vanilla is an ingredient
                                    that gives a better flavor to the
                                    cheesecake.</p>\n

                                        "http://www.chefeddy.com/2013/03/creamy-cheesecake/comment-page-1/#comment-25836">

                                        <span class=
                                        "says">said:</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t
